2:25:1429:0:14:72:507:708:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Auctions with Resale When Private Values are Uncertain: Theory and Empirical Evidence
2:26:1514:14:14:72:318:694:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Andreas Lange, John A. List, and Michael K. Price
2:27:1563:14:14:72:234:680:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 10639
2:28:1591:14:14:72:119:666:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:July 2004
2:29:1600:14:14:72:148:652:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:JEL No. L4, L7
2:30:1614:14:30:273:338:638:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:ABSTRACT
2:31:1622:30:24:72:540:608:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Auction theory is one of the richest areas of research in economics over the past three decades. Yet
2:32:1722:24:24:72:539:584:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:whether and to what extent the introduction of secondary resale markets influences bidding behavior
2:33:1821:24:24:72:540:560:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:in sealed bid first-price auctions remains under researched. This study begins by developing theory
2:34:1920:24:24:72:540:536:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:to explore auctions with resale when private values are uncertain. We put our theory to the test by
2:35:2019:24:24:72:540:512:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:examining both field data and experimental data from the lab. Our field data are from a unique data
2:36:2118:24:24:72:540:488:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:set that includes nearly 3,000 auctions (over 10,000 individual bids) for cutting rights of standing
2:37:2218:24:24:72:540:464:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:timber in British Columbia from 1996-2000. In comparing bidding patterns across agents who are
2:38:2312:24:24:72:540:440:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:likely to have resale opportunities with those who likely do not, we find evidence that is consistent
2:39:2413:24:24:72:540:416:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:with our theoretical predictions. Critical evaluation of the reduced-form bidding model, however,
2:40:2510:24:24:72:540:392:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:reveals  that  sharp  tests  of  the  theoretical  predictions  are  not  possible  because  several  other
2:41:2617:24:24:72:540:368:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:differences  may  exist  across  these  bidder  types.  We  therefore  use  a  laboratory  experiment  to
2:42:2722:24:24:72:540:344:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:examine if the resale opportunity by itself can have the predicted effect. We find that while it does
2:43:2823:24:24:72:540:320:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:have the predicted effect, a theoretical model based on risk-averse bidders explains the overall data
2:44:2924:24:24:72:540:296:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:patterns more accurately than a model based on risk-neutral  bidders.  More  generally,  the  paper
2:45:3023:24:32:72:511:272:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:highlights the inferential power of combining naturally occurring data with laboratory data.
2:46:3115:32:14:72:145:240:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Andreas Lange
2:47:3128:14:14:72:185:226:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:University of Maryland
2:48:3150:14:14:72:269:212:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Centre for European Economic Research
2:49:3187:14:14:72:175:198:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Mannheim, Germany
2:50:3204:14:28:72:179:184:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:alange@arec.umd.edu
2:51:3223:28:14:72:131:156:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:John A. List
2:52:3235:14:13:72:253:142:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Department of Economics and AREC
2:53:3267:13:14:72:161:129:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:2200 Symons Hall
2:54:3283:14:14:72:185:115:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:University of Maryland
2:55:3305:14:14:72:124:101:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:56:3313:14:0:72:166:87:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:jlist@arec.umd.edu
2:57:3331:0:14:324:391:240:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:Michael Price
2:58:3344:14:14:324:437:226:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:University of Maryland
2:59:3366:14:174:324:433:212:144:g_d0_f1:144:g_d0_f1:mprice@arec.umd.edu
3:60:3385:174:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-2- 
3:61:3389:0:20:90:172:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:I.  Introduction 
3:62:3406:20:28:126:525:688:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Auctions have a long and storied past.  From the human slave auctions carried out 
3:63:3488:28:27:90:527:660:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in  ancient  Egypt  to  the  marriage  auctions  for  brides  in  Asia  Minor  to  the  Praetorian  
3:64:3588:27:28:90:525:633:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Guard auctioning off the Roman Empire in A.D. 193, auctions have been used to allocate 
3:65:3675:28:28:90:529:605:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:goods   and   services.      While   auctions   have   certainly   served   an   important   purpose   
3:66:3778:28:27:90:526:577:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:throughout  history  and  are  now  used  to  sell  almost  anything  one  can  imagine  –  vintage  
3:67:3879:27:28:90:527:550:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:wines,  Treasury  bills,  pollution  permits,  baseball  cards,  etc.  –  economists  have  only  
3:68:3977:28:27:90:527:522:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:recently  begun  to  explore  rigorously  the  theoretical  underpinnings  of  various  auction  
3:69:4074:27:28:90:525:495:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:formats.  The seminal work is due to Vickrey, who made several contributions – deriving 
3:70:4162:28:28:90:528:467:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the  Nash  equilibrium  bidding  strategy  for  first-price  auctions,  demonstrating  revenue  
3:71:4258:28:27:90:527:439:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:equivalence,  and  proposing  the  second-price  auction  as  strategically  equivalent  to  the  
3:72:4356:27:28:89:275:412:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:English auction – in his 1961 study.1   
3:73:4396:28:27:125:526:384:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:An extensive literature examining the optimal design and application of auctions 
3:74:4477:27:28:89:527:357:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:has  since  developed.    Our  point  of  departure  in  this  study  is  to  relax  the  maintained  
3:75:4579:28:28:89:522:329:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:assumption  that  individual  valuations  are  known  with  certainty  at  the  time  of  the  first-
3:76:4680:28:27:89:525:301:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:price sealed bid auction.2  By relaxing the assumption of known use values and allowing 
3:77:4768:27:28:90:525:274:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:secondary (resale) markets, we find ourselves in an environment that is quite common in 
3:78:4856:28:27:90:529:246:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:practice.      U.S.   Forest   Service   timber   auctions,   the   procurement   of   governmental   
3:79:4958:27:50:90:527:219:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:contracts,  estate  auctions,  art  auctions,  FCC  auctions  and  the  like  all  fit  in  this  general  
3:80:5065:50:8:234:237:169:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
3:81:5113:8:16:90:525:161:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:1 This third contribution has recently been called into question by Lucking-Reiley (2000), who argues that 
3:82:5220:16:8:89:487:145:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:stamp auctioneers were using second price auctions some 65 years before Vickrey’s seminal work. 
3:83:5316:8:17:90:525:137:64:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:2 It  is  well  established  in  the  literature  that  when  bidders  receive  multi-dimensional  or  uncertain  signals,  
3:84:5439:17:12:89:525:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:auctions  may  generate  inefficient  allocations  (Pesendorfer  and  Swinkels  (2000),  Jehiel  and  Moldovanu  
3:85:5552:12:11:89:526:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:(2001),  Goeree  and  Offerman  (2003)).    Efficiency  and  bidding  strategies  in  such  an  environment  are  
3:86:5666:11:12:89:524:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:dependent upon the weight individual bidders assign to both the private and common value components of 
3:87:5769:12:11:89:524:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:a signal and upon the number of participants in a given market. However, this literature has not considered 
3:88:5877:11:36:89:226:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:the effects of secondary markets.  
4:89:5912:36:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-3- 
4:90:5916:0:27:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:class  of  allocation  mechanisms.3    Unlike  the  traditional  auction  literature  that  assumes  
4:91:6017:27:28:89:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f5:independent  private  values  (IPV)  that  are  known  with  certainty,  when  bidders  have  ex 
4:92:6114:28:27:90:527:653:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f3:ante  uncertainty  about  independent  private  values  and  anticipate  resale  opportunities,  
4:93:6211:27:28:89:528:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:equilibrium  bidding  strategies  are  dependent  upon  option  values  conveyed  from  the  
4:94:6304:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:secondary market.  Intuitively, bidder behavior in this case is fundamentally linked to the 
4:95:6396:28:27:89:341:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:existence and structure of potential resale markets.   
4:96:6451:27:28:125:529:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Our  study  attempts  to  make  both  theoretical  and empirical advances in this area.  
4:97:6540:28:27:89:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Theoretically,  we  advance  Haile  (2001,  2003)  by relaxing the maintained assumption of 
4:98:6632:27:28:89:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:risk-neutral preferences.    With  known  valuations  in  an  IPV  first  price  auction,  it  is  well  
4:99:6737:28:28:89:529:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:documented   that   risk-averse   agents   will   submit   bids   that   first-order   stochastically   
4:100:6841:28:27:89:521:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:dominate  those  of  risk-neutral  counterparts.    In  the  context  of  a  symmetric,  common-
4:101:6937:27:28:89:522:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:value  auction,  it  is  well  documented  that  risk-averse  agents  submit  bids  that  are  first-
4:102:7038:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:order  stochastically  dominated  by  a  risk-neutral  counterpart.    Since  the  auction  markets  
4:103:7139:27:28:90:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:considered  herein  contain  features  of  both  common  and  independent  private  values,  we  
4:104:7236:28:27:89:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:are a priori unable to predict the effects of risk aversion on bidder behavior without first 
4:105:7329:27:28:89:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:developing  an  extension  of  extant  theory.    By  allowing  symmetric  agents  with  CARA  
4:106:7424:28:28:89:343:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:preferences, we derive several testable implications. 
4:107:7478:28:27:125:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Our  main  empirical  objectives  are  to  (i)  evaluate  the  validity  of  our  theoretical  
4:108:7573:27:28:89:527:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:model  of  auctions  with  resale,  and  (ii)  provide  empirical  evidence  of  behavior  in  such  
4:109:7674:28:27:89:527:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:markets  that  can  aid  in  the  design  and  implementation  of  efficient  mechanisms  for  the  
4:110:7774:27:37:89:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:allocation of goods and services.  To achieve these objectives, we combine insights from 
4:111:7863:37:7:234:237:120:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
4:112:7911:7:16:90:525:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:3 There is a growing theoretical literature that examines the impacts of such resale opportunities on bidder 
4:113:8020:16:12:89:526:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:behavior  and  a  seller’s  optimal  choice  of  auction  format  (see,  for  example,  Bikhchandani  and  Huang  
4:114:8134:12:11:89:526:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:(1989),  Gupta  and  Lebrun  (1999),  Haile  (2000,  2001,  2003),  Troger  (2003),  and  Garratt  and  Troger  
4:115:8246:11:36:89:124:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:(2003)). 
5:116:8255:36:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-4- 
5:117:8259:0:27:90:530:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:naturally  occurring  data  with  insights  gained  from  a  controlled  laboratory  experiment.    
5:118:8359:27:28:90:527:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:One  benefit  of  our  approach  is  that  it  enables  a  comparison  of  behavior  across  two  
5:119:8457:28:27:90:415:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:different environments with varying levels of control and realism.   
5:120:8526:27:28:126:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Our  naturally  occurring  data  are  drawn  from  nearly  3,000  timber  auctions  (over  
5:121:8617:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:10,000 individual bids) from the Small Business Forest Enterprise Program (SBFEP) for 
5:122:8703:28:27:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the interior region of British Columbia (BC) for the period 1996-2000.  These data can be 
5:123:8793:27:28:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:viewed as extending the empirical findings in Haile (2001), who used U.S. timber auction 
5:124:8882:28:27:90:528:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:data to explore bidding behavior before and after a federal regulation that allowed resale.  
5:125:8975:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Unlike his temporal identification strategy, our identification rests on static comparisons 
5:126:9067:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:between bidding patterns of three very different bidder groups:  loggers on the coast and 
5:127:9157:28:27:89:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:interior  of  BC  and  mills  located  in  the  BC  interior.    While  we  find  evidence  consonant  
5:128:9260:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:with our theoretical predictions and in line with Haile’s (2001) findings, we are cautious 
5:129:9351:28:27:89:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:to make strong inference because exact comparisons cannot be unequivocally made.  As 
5:130:9436:27:28:89:530:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in   Haile’s   (2001)   study,   where   several   identification   assumptions   are   necessarily   
5:131:9538:28:27:89:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:imposed,  in  our  case  variations  in  the  underlying  valuations,  risk  posture,  and  structure  
5:132:9641:27:28:89:529:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:(nature)  of  secondary  markets  are  largely  unobserved  and  therefore  may  frustrate  
5:133:9733:28:28:89:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:appropriate  inference.    This  fact  highlights  the  difficulty  of  evaluating  the  impacts  of  
5:134:9835:28:27:89:370:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:resale on bidder behavior using uncontrolled field data.     
5:135:9896:27:28:125:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:One way to approach this quandary is to make use of a laboratory experiment.  By 
5:136:9977:28:27:89:524:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:studying artificial markets that differ only in whether a secondary market is available, we 
5:137:10069:27:28:89:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:are  permitted  a  unique  insight  into  whether  the  resale  market  by  itself  can  lead  to  such  
5:138:10174:28:28:89:527:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:predicted  consequences.    Experimental  methods  thus  allow  us  to  study  the  effects  of  
5:139:10271:28:63:89:524:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:resale possibilities that would be difficult to identify in naturally occurring data.  Keeping 
6:140:10366:63:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-5- 
6:141:10370:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:an  eye  toward  designing  a  laboratory  setting  that  resembles  naturally  occurring  markets  
6:142:10470:27:28:90:522:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:while  maintaining  a  strong  theoretical  link,  we  designed  an  experiment  using  the  first-
6:143:10569:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:price auction with both a second stage optimal auction (OA) as well as an English auction 
6:144:10659:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:(EA) continuation game of complete information.  This particular design choice allows a 
6:145:10747:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:controlled test of existing theory and a useful benchmark for making inference from field 
6:146:10837:28:27:90:527:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:data, since the secondary market in BC most likely lies within these two market extremes.  
6:147:10928:27:28:126:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The  lab  results  are  broadly  in  line  with  theoretical  expectations.    We  find  that  
6:148:11023:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:experimental  subjects  submit  bids  that  are  significantly  higher  in  markets  with  resale  
6:149:11122:27:28:90:528:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:organized  by  an  optimal  auction  than  in  those  without  such  opportunity  (or  with  
6:150:11215:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:secondary  markets  organized  by  an  EA).    An  interesting  data  pattern  not  anticipated  by  
6:151:11316:28:27:90:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:extant theory is that over lower ranges of the signal space, realized bids are less than the 
6:152:11409:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:risk-neutral theoretical predictions, while over higher ranges of the signal space, realized 
6:153:11502:28:27:90:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bids  are  greater  than  the  risk-neutral  theoretical  predictions.    Yet  these  tendencies  are  
6:154:11605:27:28:90:448:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:consonant with our theory of bidding by agents with CARA preferences.   
6:155:11677:28:27:126:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The remainder of the paper is crafted as follows.  Section II provides an overview 
6:156:11760:27:28:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of  the  SBFEP  auction  market  and  our  strategy  for  identifying  resale  differences  using  
6:157:11859:28:28:90:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:reduced-form  bid  functions.    Section  III  develops  a  theory  of  bidding  by  agents  with  
6:158:11958:28:27:90:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:CARA  preferences  in  auction  markets  that  parallel  our  laboratory  setting.    Section  IV  
6:159:12057:27:28:90:430:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:discusses the laboratory experiment and results.  Section V concludes. 
6:160:12128:28:28:90:254:184:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:II. The SBFEP Auction Market 
6:161:12157:28:27:90:340:156:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:The SBFEP Auction – Background and Predictions 
6:162:12204:27:28:126:526:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Our  naturally  occurring  data  are  drawn  from  nearly  3,000  timber  auctions  (over  
6:163:12295:28:63:90:524:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:12,000 individual bids) from the British Columbia SBFEP for the period 1996-2000 – the 
7:164:12382:63:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-6- 
7:165:12386:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:identical  data  set  that  BC  is  using  to  begin  its  new  pricing  approach  under  the  changed  
7:166:12490:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:circumstance  agreement  for  the  U.S.-Canadian  softwood  lumber  dispute.4  To examine 
7:167:12580:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the effects of ex post resale opportunities on bidder behavior, we compare reduced-form 
7:168:12668:27:28:89:524:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bid functions across distinct subsets of bidders that face different market conditions.  Our 
7:169:12761:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:general  approach  is  in  the  spirit  of,  for  example,  Porter  and  Zona  (1999),  in  that  we  
7:170:12863:28:27:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:employ  reduced-form  methods  to  infer  the  nature  of  resale  effects  from  differences  in  
7:171:12962:27:28:89:301:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidding patterns across subsets of bidders.   
7:172:13008:28:27:125:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:SBFEP auctions in BC allocate standing timber of less than 50,000 metric board 
7:173:13087:27:28:89:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:feet  cubed  (mb3)  to  small  logging  companies  and  contractors.    SBFEP  timber  sales  
7:174:13181:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:account for approximately 13 percent of the harvested timber in the province.  About half 
7:175:13271:28:27:89:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of this timber is allocated via sealed bid tenders to the highest bidder under section 20 of 
7:176:13364:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the province’s Forest Act.  These auctions are subdivided into two types: Category 1 and 
7:177:13453:28:27:89:524:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Category 2, where Category 1 auctions include only market loggers.  Category 2 auctions 
7:178:13541:27:28:89:521:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:are open to both registered market loggers and registered owners of processing facilities.  
7:179:13633:28:27:125:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Category 1 bidders purchase timber cutting rights and sell harvested timber to end 
7:180:13716:27:28:89:527:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:users.    In  the  interior  of  BC  almost  all  harvested  timber  is  sold  to  either  major  forest  
7:181:13822:28:28:89:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:license  holders  or  local  sawmills.    Ex  ante,  bidders  contract  with  a  prospective  buyer  to  
7:182:13927:28:27:89:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:arrange  an  agreement  in  principle  to  sell/buy  if  they  win  the  auction.    The  bidders  then  
7:183:14032:27:28:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:submit bids and the winner consummates the agreement in principle and chooses to lock 
7:184:14118:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in  the  stumpage  price  he  bid.    In  the  coastal  region  of  BC,  Category  1  bidders  ex  ante  
7:185:14223:27:71:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:contract  with  prospective  buyers  to  deliver  a  portion  of  harvested  timber  and  sell  the  
7:186:14324:71:8:234:237:86:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
7:187:14372:8:40:90:406:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:4 See Price and List (2004) for a discussion of the solution to the trade dispute. 
8:188:14455:40:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-7- 
8:189:14459:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:remaining harvested timber on the Vancouver log market.5  Category 2 bidders purchase 
8:190:14545:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:timber  cutting  rights  to  obtain  raw  materials  for  their  processing  operations.    Bidders  
8:191:14646:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:either process harvested timber or trade it to obtain needed materials.  Since both loggers 
8:192:14738:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:along  the  coast  and  processing  facilities  are  actively  engaged  in  the  ex  post  buying  and  
8:193:14842:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:selling  of  harvested  logs  whereas  loggers  in  the  interior  contract  ex  ante  to  deliver  all  
8:194:14947:28:27:89:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:harvest to a given buyer, we believe that resale might enter into the bidding strategies of 
8:195:15039:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the former but not the latter.  Intuitively, since the former set of bidders have an outside 
8:196:15132:28:27:89:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:option  to  sell  logs  on  a  spot  market  whereas  the  latter  do  not  have  such  an  option,  one  
8:197:15238:27:28:89:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:would expect that loggers from the coast and processing facilities would provide an upper 
8:198:15328:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:envelope  on  the  observed  bids  of  loggers  from  the  interior.    It  is  thus  hypothesized  that  
8:199:15434:28:27:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bids  should  differ  across  these  groups  in  the  direction  that  theory  predicts.    To  identify  
8:200:15540:27:28:90:411:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:whether this effect holds, we rely upon cross sectional variation.6   
8:201:15610:28:29:90:386:377:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Identifying Resale Effects from Reduced-Form Bid Functions

8:212:16187:8:16:90:525:138:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:5 Along the interior region of BC, no spot market for logs has developed due to differences in infrastructure 
8:213:16297:16:8:89:440:122:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:and associated transportation costs that limit the profitability of spot market exchange.  
8:214:16388:8:17:90:526:114:64:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:6 In  this  sense,  our  identification  strategy  is  much  different  from  Haile  (2001),  who  analyzes  individual  
8:215:16508:17:12:90:526:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:bids  from  the  U.S.  timber  auctions  and  makes  use  of  the  temporal  variation  in  the  imposition  of  federal

8:217:16753:11:36:90:323:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:comparing them to bids after the regulations took effect.   
9:218:16813:36:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-8- 
9:219:16817:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Without resale, firm i’s expected profits depend on its own (expected) value of the good 
9:220:16906:27:31:90:339:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:given its characteristics, t(xi), and are thus given by 
9:221:16962:31:31:189:557:650:186:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:()(),;()()−=−iii   iiii  iibxBtx   bQbπ.                                                            (2II)            
9:222:17079:31:27:126:526:619:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A  competitive  bidder  derives  an  optimal  bid  strategy  conditional  upon  his  likely  
9:223:17172:27:28:90:526:592:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:valuation  and  some  probability  distribution  over  the  valuations  (and  hence  bids)  of  all  
9:224:17273:28:27:90:524:564:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:possible competitors.  In equilibrium, this imposes a structure on the relationship between 
9:225:17365:27:28:90:525:537:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:a  given  firm’s  bid  and  the  probability  of  that  bid  winning  the  auction.    However,  when  
9:226:17468:28:28:90:527:509:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidders  have  resale  opportunities,  equation  (2)  must  be  adjusted  to  reflect  expected  
9:227:17565:28:27:90:525:481:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:profits  from  resale  trade.    For  example,  when  the  second-stage  continuation  game  is  an  
9:228:17666:27:28:90:526:454:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:optimal  auction  with  complete  information,  the  winning  bidder  obtains  in  equilibrium  a  
9:229:17765:28:27:90:525:426:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:payoff equal to the highest use value among all players, minus the price paid to the initial 
9:230:17858:27:30:90:447:399:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:seller.  In such an environment, firm i’s expected profits are thus given by 
9:231:17935:30:34:247:524:369:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                ()()()1,;−=−iii   ii  iibxBt  b Q bπ,      (2II’) 
9:232:18031:34:30:90:525:335:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:where t1 is the highest use value among all bidders in the auction and Qi(bi) is again the 
9:233:18122:30:28:89:525:305:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:probability that bidder i wins the auction.  Haile (2003) examines bidder behavior in such 
9:234:18213:28:27:90:529:277:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:situations  and  shows  that  optimal  bid  strategies  in  first-price  auctions  with  resale  
9:235:18310:27:28:90:526:250:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:represented  by  an  OA  continuation  game  differ  from  those  of  an  equivalent  first-price  
9:236:18409:28:27:90:529:222:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:auction   without   resale.      Across   all   signal   (valuation)   ranges,   bids   in   the   former   
9:237:18517:27:28:90:328:195:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:environment weakly dominate those in the latter. 
9:238:18566:28:28:126:526:167:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: To identify resale effects, we employ a general approach that is in the spirit of, for 
9:239:18653:28:27:90:526:139:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:example, Porter and Zona (1993, 1999).  We employ reduced-form methods to infer the 
9:240:18737:27:28:90:526:112:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:nature  of  resale  effects  by  differences  in  bidding  patterns  across  subsets  of  firms  facing  
9:241:18842:28:46:90:527:84:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:different  outside  options.    Our  identification  strategy  characterizes  equilibrium  bidding  
10:242:18942:46:0:298:315:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-9- 
10:243:18946:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:behavior as a function of both observed and unobserved auction-specific and firm effects 
10:244:19035:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:assumed to affect firm i’s valuation and/or probability of winning a given auction.  Once 
10:245:19125:28:27:90:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:an  equilibrium  bid  function  has  been  specified,  a  pooled  regression  model  for  the  set  of  
10:246:19229:27:28:90:529:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:coastal  Category  1,  interior  Category  1,  and  Category  2  bids  is  estimated  using  
10:247:19322:28:28:90:524:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:interaction effects for these distinct subsets of bidders.  Theoretically, if resale effects are 
10:248:19419:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:present in the Category 2 and coastal bids, then parameter estimates from the interaction 
10:249:19509:27:28:90:527:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of  these  groupings  with  observed  auction  covariates  should  differ  from  those  of  the  
10:250:19606:28:27:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:model covariates for interior loggers.  In particular, we should observe that the estimated 
10:251:19698:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:comparative static effect of competition on observed bids is smaller for interior Category 
10:252:19789:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:1 auctions than it is for otherwise equivalent Category 2 or coastal Category 1 auctions.     
10:253:19883:28:27:126:524:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Specifically, assume that equilibrium bidding behavior for symmetric, risk-neutral 
10:254:19966:27:32:90:435:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:agents in a first-price sealed bid auction follows the linear specification 
10:255:20042:32:28:299:553:373:49:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f3:ijijijXPεβ+=,                                                                                                (3II)            
10:256:20168:28:28:90:525:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:where Pij is the ith bidder’s bonus bid in auction j.  Xij is a set of regressors underlying the 
10:257:20265:28:29:90:525:317:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f3:ith firm’s valuation for tract j plus a set of interaction terms between these regressors and 
10:258:20359:29:29:90:525:288:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:dummy  variables  for  coastal  loggers  and  mills;  εij  =  αi  +  uij;  E[αi]  =  0,  E[αi2]  =  σα2,

10:260:20571:28:28:90:521:231:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:assumed  to  capture  heterogeneity  that  would  be  left  uncontrolled  in  a  standard  cross-

10:262:20687:28:27:90:312:175:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The SBFEP Auction Data - Empirical Results 
10:263:20729:27:28:125:525:148:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:We  observe  2,671  (247)  SBFEP  sealed-bid  tender  first-price  auctions  conducted  
10:264:20817:28:27:89:525:120:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in the interior (coast) of British Columbia for the period January 1996 through December 
10:265:20906:27:55:89:529:93:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:2002.    These  auctions  provide  more  than  11,500  individual  bids,  from  which  we  
11:266:20997:55:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-10- 
11:267:21002:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:eliminate any bids submitted in auctions with only a single bidder, any bids submitted by 
11:268:21092:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:a  suspected  cartel  firm,  any  bids  submitted  in  an  auction  with  an  estimated  net  cruise  
11:269:21194:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:volume of less than 1,000 mb3, and any bids submitted in an auction employing a format 
11:270:21281:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:other than a first-price sealed tender.  This results in a sample of nearly 1,300 firms that 
11:271:21374:28:28:90:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:submit  nearly  5,700  bids  for  the  interior  and  a  sample  of  nearly  475  firms  that  submit  
11:272:21477:28:27:90:252:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:nearly 1500 bids on the coast.7     
11:273:21513:27:28:126:527:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:To  generate  the  data  for  the  empirical  model,  we  combine  information  from  a  
11:274:21602:28:27:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:number of sources.  First, a list of all bidders currently registered to participate in SBFEP 
11:275:21696:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:timber auctions was provided by the Ministry of Forests (MOF) in BC.  This listing was 
11:276:21783:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:used to generate unique identification codes for each bidder in the data set.  Second, the 
11:277:21874:28:27:90:528:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:MOF  provided  bid  sheets  for  each  of  the  2,918  auctions.    The  bid  sheets  provide  
11:278:21969:27:28:90:526:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:information  on  (i)  the  regional  office  holding  and  date  of  the  auction,  (ii)  the  estimated  
11:279:22075:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:net cruise volume of timber on the plot, (iii) the announced upset rate for the auction, and 
11:280:22168:27:28:89:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:(iv)  the  identity  and  bonus  bid  per  metric  board  feet  cubed  for  each  participant  in  the  
11:281:22272:28:27:89:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:auction.  Finally, the MOF provided a database that contains detailed information on the 
11:282:22361:27:28:89:234:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:characteristics of each plot.8   
11:283:22394:28:28:126:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:To  condition  behavior  on  observed  auction  characteristics  in  tests  for  resale  
11:284:22483:28:27:89:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:effects, we estimate a series of reduced-form bid functions.  Specifically, we assume that 
11:285:22574:27:28:89:529:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:equilibrium  bidding  behavior  follows  the  linear  specification  in  equation  (3),  and  
11:286:22668:28:31:89:184:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:therefore estimate

12:292:23183:36:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-11-

12:294:23291:27:29:90:183:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:regressors include: 
12:295:23311:29:14:108:412:652:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Mills – dummy variable that equals 1 if the bidder is a mill 
12:296:23373:14:15:108:455:638:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Coast – dummy variable that equals 1 if the bidder is from the coast 
12:297:23443:15:15:108:328:623:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Upset – the announced upset rate per mb3 
12:298:23484:15:14:108:302:608:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Upset2 – the square of the upset rate 
12:299:23523:14:15:108:341:594:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Bidders – the number of bidders in auction j 
12:300:23569:15:15:108:353:579:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Bidders2 – the square of the number of bidders 
12:301:23617:15:14:108:358:564:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• NCV – the announced net cruise volume in mb3 
12:302:23662:14:15:108:393:550:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• NCV2 – the square of the announced net cruise volume 
12:303:23716:15:15:108:459:535:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Coast_upset – an interaction of the coastal dummy and the upset rate 
12:304:23786:15:14:108:428:520:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Coast_upset2 – an interaction of the coastal dummy and upset2

12:307:23979:15:14:108:413:476:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Coast_ncv – an interaction of the coastal dummy and NCV 
12:308:24036:14:14:108:420:462:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:• Coast_ncv2 – an interaction of the coastal dummy and NCV2 
12:309:24094:14:14:108:111:448:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: 
12:310:24094:14:27:90:527:434:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Table  1  provides  parameter  estimates  for  equation  (4)  estimated  for  the  set  of  7,185  
12:311:24193:27:28:90:325:407:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:observations across a number of specifications.   
12:312:24243:28:28:126:526:379:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:  Empirical  results  for  the  pooled  model  in  Table  1  are  consistent  with  economic  
12:313:24337:28:27:90:526:351:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:intuition.  First, since we consider SBFEP auctions as first-price IPV sealed bid tenders, 
12:314:24428:27:28:90:526:324:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:economic  theory  predicts  that  bids  should  increase  in  the  number  of  bidders  over  the  
12:315:24527:28:27:90:525:296:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:relevant range (n=15 (n=18) is the boundary for the number of auction participants in the 
12:316:24617:27:28:90:525:269:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:interior (on the coast).9  The positive and significant coefficient on the number of bidders 
12:317:24710:28:28:90:524:241:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:across all model specifications is consistent with this prediction.  Second, bidders respond 
12:318:24803:28:27:90:525:213:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:positively to the announced upset rate.  Since the announced upset rate is correlated with 
12:319:24894:27:66:90:527:186:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the value a bidder assigns to a given tract, this finding is consistent with economic theory.  
12:320:24989:66:7:234:237:120:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
12:321:25037:7:16:90:526:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:9  We  follow  Haile  (2001)  and  Athey  and  Levin  (2001)  in  assuming  these  are  IPV  auctions.    This  is  
12:322:25153:16:12:89:524:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:intuitively appealing for these data considering that bidders face different capacity constraints (and possibly 
12:323:25265:12:11:90:525:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:possess different technologies), suggesting that idiosyncratic, firm-specific cost factors are more important 
12:324:25375:11:36:90:232:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:than plot-specific, uncertain costs.  
13:325:25413:36:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-12- 
13:326:25418:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Finally,  there  are  temporal  effects  in  bidder  behavior.    Across  all  model  specifications,  
13:327:25521:27:28:90:507:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the inclusion of fixed year effects improves the overall predictive power of our model. 
13:328:25609:28:27:126:527:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:  Empirical  results  presented  in  Table  1  suggest  an  important  difference  in  the  
13:329:25701:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:behavior  of  mills  and  loggers  along  the  coast  relative  to  loggers  in  the  interior  that  are  
13:330:25808:28:28:90:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:suggestive  of  resale  for  the  former  set  of  bidders:    measured  at  the  sample  means,  the  
13:331:25911:28:27:90:527:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:estimated  marginal  effect  of  adding  an  additional  bidder  in  an  auction  for  our  fully  
13:332:26010:27:28:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:interactive model specification (F) with year fixed effects is approximately 47.16 percent 
13:333:26101:28:27:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:($2.259 to $1.535) greater for Category 2 auctions than it is for Category 1 auctions.  For 
13:334:26193:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Category  1  bidders  along  the  coast,  this  estimated  difference  is  30.29  percent  ($2.00  to  
13:335:26296:28:28:90:527:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:$1.535).    These  estimates  are  consistent  with  resale  opportunities  for  the  former  set  of  
13:336:26399:28:27:90:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidders and not for the latter.  Equilibrium bidding strategies in auctions with resale are 
13:337:26491:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:conditioned upon information related to other bidders in the market that is absent in the 
13:338:26581:28:27:90:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:strategy  of  a  firm  bidding  in  a  market  without  resale.    Hence,  we  would  expect  greater  
13:339:26684:27:28:90:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:competition  in  the  former  case  when  the  secondary  market  institution  is  an  OA  
13:340:26775:28:27:90:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:continuation  game  of  complete  information  (or  a  similar  analog),  as  we  assume  for  the  
13:341:26875:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Category 2 mills and Category 1 loggers along the coast.  This finding is consonant with 
13:342:26964:28:28:89:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the predictions and analysis employed by Haile (2001) to identify resale effects for U.S. 
13:343:27054:28:27:89:524:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:timber auctions.  Combined with other parameter estimates in Table 1 (e.g., the estimated 
13:344:27144:27:28:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:parametric shifter terms in the model), we take the empirical results to suggest that resale 
13:345:27237:28:28:89:452:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:opportunities influence bidding in the direction that theory would predict.   
13:346:27315:28:27:90:405:156:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:III. Risk, Resale, and Bidder Behavior – First-Price Auctions 
13:347:27377:27:28:126:527:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:  Although  we  are  able  to  extend  the  empirical  findings  of  Haile  (2001)  and  
13:348:27466:28:63:90:528:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:identify  empirical  differences  across  bidders  indicative  of  the  predicted  comparative  
14:349:27562:63:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-13- 
14:350:27567:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:static  effects  of  resale  opportunities  on  bids,  the  field  data  on  SBFEP  auctions  do  not  
14:351:27670:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:allow us to control properly for many underlying determinants like the (expected) value 
14:352:27758:28:27:90:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:from  using  the  good,  the  division  of  surplus  on  the  resale  market,  or  the  risk-posture  of  
14:353:27864:27:28:90:529:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the  firms.10    The  effects  of  resale  are  inferred  from  differences  in  reduced-form  
14:354:27959:28:28:90:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:parameters  across  the  subsets  of  bidders.    Such  analysis  is  sensitive  to  issues  of  model  
14:355:28063:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:specification and the interpretation of estimated parameters.  In practice, both the “true” 
14:356:28155:27:28:90:528:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:underlying  model  specification  and  its  associated  interpretation  are  unknown  and/or  
14:357:28249:28:27:90:528:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:unobserved  in  naturally  occurring  data.    While  one  may  report  empirical  evidence  
14:358:28342:27:28:89:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:consistent with the predicted comparative static effects of resale, to make more powerful 
14:359:28432:28:28:89:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:inference of whether such differences are in fact generated by the existence and nature of 
14:360:28523:28:27:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:secondary  markets,  one  can  examine  behavior  in  a  controlled  environment.    We  follow  
14:361:28620:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:this line of reasoning and complement the field results with lab experiments.  To derive 
14:362:28709:28:27:90:447:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:testable predictions, we first develop a model that allows risk aversion.11   
14:363:28787:27:28:126:521:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Consider  a  first-price  auction  with  resale  opportunities  with  n  symmetric,  risk-
14:364:28877:28:27:90:527:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:averse  players.    We  assume  that  players  are  risk  averse  with  constant  absolute  risk  
14:365:28975:27:48:90:530:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:aversion   (CARA).      That   is,   the   von-Neumann-Morgenstern   utility   is   given   by   
14:366:29072:48:8:234:237:247:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
14:367:29120:8:16:90:526:239:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:10  For  example,  there  is  a  possibility  that  loggers  are  able  to  mitigate  risk  in  the  field  by  entering  into  
14:368:29248:16:11:89:525:223:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:contractual  relationships  with  processors  and/or  logging  companies  that  Category  2  bidders  are  unable  to  
14:369:29367:11:12:89:524:212:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:mitigate.  If so, then one could argue that loggers are less risk averse than are mills.  Hence, it is possible 
14:370:29479:12:11:89:524:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:that estimated differences in behavior across these two groups are generated by differences in unobserved 
14:371:29585:11:7:89:356:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:risk posture rather than differences in ex post resale opportunities. 
14:372:29655:7:16:90:525:182:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:11  As  noted  by  Haile  (2003),  auction  markets  with  resale  have  components  of  both  common  and  private  
14:373:29772:16:12:90:522:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:value  auctions.    It  is  well  documented  in  the  experimental  literature  that  in  a  private  value  setting  risk-
14:374:29896:12:11:90:525:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:averse agents submit bids that first-order stochastically dominate those of risk-neutral agents.  In common 
14:375:30004:11:12:90:525:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:value  settings,  however,  this  tendency  is  reversed.    Risk-averse  agents  in  a  common  value  auction  submit  
14:376:30125:12:11:90:526:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:bids  that  are  stochastically  dominated  by  risk-neutral  counterparts.    Given  the  persistence  of  risk-averse  
14:377:30246:11:12:90:524:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:behavior on the part of student subjects in the lab, and lacking an a priori theoretical prediction/conjecture 
14:378:30357:12:11:90:525:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:about the effects of risk aversion on behavior in our setting, it is important to develop such theory to enable 
14:379:30469:11:12:90:525:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:us to filter out the effects of risk aversion from those of resale opportunity.  Without such theory, empirical 
14:380:30581:12:11:90:468:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:tests are potentially confounded and do not permit a direct test of our desired treatment effect.

17:562:34118:28:27:89:288:513:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Bidder Behavior in Auctions with Resale 
17:563:34158:27:28:125:525:486:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Whenever a player can resell a commodity won at auction on a secondary market, 
17:564:34237:28:27:89:525:458:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the value the bidder places on the commodity in the primary auction market depends on 
17:565:34323:27:28:89:526:431:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the  price  at  which  resale  can  take  place.  As  discussed  in  Haile  (2003),  such  prices  are  
17:566:34427:28:28:89:528:403:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:dependent  upon  the  informational  structure  and  trading  institution  assumed  on  the  
17:567:34520:28:27:89:186:375:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:secondary market.   
17:568:34540:27:28:125:526:348:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:We first study the case of complete information on a resale market characterized 
17:569:34621:28:27:89:527:320:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:by  an  OA  continuation  game,  i.e.,  we  assume  that  use  values  are  common  knowledge  
17:570:34716:27:28:89:526:293:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:among  players  and  that  the  seller  extracts  the  entire  surplus  by  selling  to  the  opponent  
17:571:34820:28:27:89:485:265:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:with the highest use value on the resale market whenever such trade is profitable.  
17:572:34904:27:28:125:524:238:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Let us denote the distribution of use values of a player given that her signal is less 
17:573:34991:28:38:89:192:210:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:than or equal to y as

22:955:40924:28:28:89:411:647:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Implications for Optimal Bidding Strategies: Resale vs. No Resale 
22:956:40990:28:27:126:529:619:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:First,  note  that  for  infinitely  high  risk  aversion,  bids  converge  towards  the

22:960:41273:27:28:89:525:505:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Hence, since a large majority of agents in the population are risk averse, the differences 
22:961:41364:28:27:89:529:477:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:due  to  the  possibility  of  resale  are  generally  overstated  if  only  risk  neutrality  is  
22:962:41463:27:39:89:150:450:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:considered.

22:983:41828:45:28:89:525:261:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:which  coincides  with  the  bid  function  for  markets  without  resale.    The  intuition  behind  
22:984:41930:28:28:89:525:233:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:this result is that with resale opportunities an agent wins the auction only if she receives 
22:985:42023:28:27:90:528:205:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the  highest  signal,  i.e.,  she  has  the  largest  use  value.    The  resale  value,  therefore,

22:987:42215:28:27:90:526:150:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:signal, however, resale generally increases signals since the expected resale value is not 
22:988:42306:27:28:90:323:123:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:smaller than the expected use value of an agent. 
22:989:42355:28:57:90:442:95:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Implications for Optimal Bidding Strategies: The Effect of Risk Aversion 
23:990:42428:57:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-22- 
23:991:42433:0:28:125:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The  qualitative  effects  of  risk  aversion  depend  on  whether  the  risk-neutral  bids  
23:992:42526:28:30:89:525:680:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:exceed or equal the minimal use value given by min()ux, which depends on the specific 
23:993:42612:30:29:90:525:650:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:distributions of use values and signals.  However, the following cases might occur for a 
23:994:42701:29:33:90:221:621:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:treatment {},,∈tNOAEA: 
23:995:42724:33:17:90:526:588:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:1. Under  risk  neutrality,  min()()>tbx   u   x:  Risk  aversion  decreases  bids  for  high  degrees  
23:996:42827:17:15:108:189:571:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of risk aversion. 
23:997:42845:15:17:90:486:556:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:2. Under risk neutrality, min()()<tbx   u   x: Risk aversion eventually increases bids. 
23:998:42932:17:14:90:93:539:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: 
23:999:42932:14:27:107:525:525:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:In our experimental markets described below, case 1 holds for small signals whereas 
23:1000:43016:27:28:90:528:498:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:case  2  applies  to  larger  signals.    The  effects  of  risk  aversion  therefore  qualitatively  
23:1001:43118:28:28:90:525:470:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:change over the range of signals.  In our experimental markets, we would thus predict a 
23:1002:43206:28:27:90:526:442:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:crossing  of  optimal  bid  functions  for  both  the  resale  and  no-resale  treatments  for  agents  
23:1003:43310:27:28:90:315:415:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:that demonstrate high levels of risk aversion.   
23:1004:43359:28:28:90:434:387:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Implications for Optimal Bidding Strategies: Minimal Observable Bids 
23:1005:43428:28:27:126:524:359:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The minimal bids in both resale and no-resale cases are given by the lowest signal 
23:1006:43511:27:28:90:493:332:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:type.  Note that, using l’Hospital’s rule again, the equilibrium bid functions lead to

24:1024:44038:52:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-23- 
24:1025:44043:0:27:90:286:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:IV. Experimental Design and Results  
24:1026:44080:27:28:90:194:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Experimental Design 
24:1027:44099:28:27:126:528:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:  A  total  of  90  subjects  participated  in  our  laboratory  experiment,  which  was  
24:1028:44189:27:28:90:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:conducted during the Fall 2003 and Spring 2004 semesters at the University of Maryland 
24:1029:44276:28:28:90:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in  College  Park.    Each  session  consisted  of  two  experimental  parts:  a  first-price  auction  
24:1030:44380:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:market  with  or  without  resale  opportunity  and  the  Holt  and  Laury  (2002)  experimental  
24:1031:44478:27:28:90:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:procedure  to  elicit  the  risk  preference  of  each  participant.    Each  part  of  the  laboratory  
24:1032:44583:28:27:90:257:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:experiment is described below.      
24:1033:44619:27:28:90:248:488:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Part I: The Auction Market         
24:1034:44654:28:28:126:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Each  subject’s  experience  typically  followed  four  steps:  (1)  consideration  of  an  
24:1035:44746:28:27:90:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:invitation to participate in an experiment, (2) learning the auction rules, (3) actual market 
24:1036:44840:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:participation, and (4) conclusion of the experiment and completion of the Holt and Laury 
24:1037:44929:28:27:90:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:(2002)  risk-aversion  experiment.    In  Step  1,  undergraduate  students  from  the  University  
24:1038:45029:27:28:90:529:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of  Maryland  were  recruited  using  e-mail  solicitations  and  flyers  hung  in  academic  
24:1039:45123:28:27:90:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:buildings across the campus.  Once the prerequisite number of subjects had responded, a 
24:1040:45211:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:second e-mail was sent to each participant inviting them to participate in an experimental 
24:1041:45302:28:28:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:session to be held at a given date/time.  After subjects were seated in a room, in Step 2 a 
24:1042:45394:28:27:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:monitor thoroughly explained the experimental instructions and auction rules (included in 
24:1043:45484:27:28:90:205:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Appendices B and C).   
24:1044:45507:28:27:126:528:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Before  proceeding,  a  few  key  aspects  of  the  experimental  design  should  be  
24:1045:45593:27:28:90:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:highlighted.    First,  all  bidders  were  informed  that  earnings  from  the  auction  experiment  
24:1046:45695:28:28:90:527:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:would  be  added  to  earnings  from  a  second,  unrelated  experiment  to  determine  total  
24:1047:45790:28:63:90:526:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:earnings for the session.  Second, individuals were informed that they would be bidders 
25:1048:45878:63:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-24- 
25:1049:45883:0:27:89:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:in  the  experiment.    In  each  of  the  12  rounds  (2  practice  and  10  that  count  towards  
25:1050:45983:27:28:89:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:earnings),  they  would  be  given  a  bidder’s  card  that  contained  a  number,  known  only  to  
25:1051:46084:28:27:89:530:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:that  bidder,  representing  a  signal  of  the  value  of  one  unit  of  the  fictitious  commodity.    
25:1052:46190:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Importantly,  all  agents  were  informed  that  this  information  was  strictly  private  and  that  
25:1053:46293:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:both  signals  and  use  values  would  change  each  round.    They  were  also  informed  about  
25:1054:46392:28:27:89:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the number of other bidders in the market (4), that they would bid against the same four 
25:1055:46481:27:28:89:484:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidders for all ten rounds, and that agents may have different signals (use values). 
25:1056:46566:28:27:126:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Third, the monitor explained how signals were determined in each market period 
25:1057:46645:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:and how these signals related to the agent’s final reservation (use) value.  Subjects were 
25:1058:46736:28:28:90:530:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:informed  that  in  each  period,  they  would  receive  a  signal  from  the  interval  [$0,  $50].    
25:1059:46840:28:27:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:These  signals  were  determined  by  adding  a  random  integer  generated  from  a  uniform  
25:1060:46935:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:distribution on the interval [-$10, $10] to the agent’s final use value which was itself an 
25:1061:47027:28:27:90:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:integer  value  randomly  drawn  on  the  uniform  interval  [$10,  $40].    Several  examples  
25:1062:47123:27:28:90:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:illustrated  the  relationship  between  a  given  use  value  and  the  range  of  signals  that  the  
25:1063:47227:28:27:90:393:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidder could receive in the first stage, and vice versa.                
25:1064:47299:27:28:126:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Fourth, the monitor explained how earnings were determined.  In the baseline, no 
25:1065:47380:28:28:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:resale treatment, the highest bidder earns the difference between their end use value and 
25:1066:47470:28:27:90:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:their  bid.    All  other  bidders  earn  zero.    In  the  resale  treatment  with  OA  continuation  
25:1067:47573:27:28:90:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:game,  the  bidder  who  submits  the  highest  bid  earns  the  difference  between  the  highest  
25:1068:47673:28:27:90:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:use  value  of  all  bidders  and  the  winning  bid.    All  other  bidders  earn  zero.    In  the  resale  
25:1069:47783:27:28:90:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:treatment  with  EA  continuation  game,  the  bidder  who  submits  the  highest  bid  receives  
25:1070:47881:28:28:90:525:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the maximum of her use value and the second highest use value of all participants minus 
25:1071:47969:28:63:90:525:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:her  winning  bid.    The  bidder  who  does  not  submit  the  high  bid  but  has  the  highest  use  
26:1072:48073:63:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-25- 
26:1073:48078:0:27:89:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:value  receives  the  difference  between  this  value  and  the  second  highest  use  value  of  all  
26:1074:48182:27:28:90:527:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:other  participants.    All  other  bidders  earn  zero  for  the  round.    Total  earnings  for  each  
26:1075:48287:28:27:90:437:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:treatment are computed by summing the earnings across the 10 periods. 
26:1076:48357:27:28:126:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:In  the  resale  treatment  with  OA  continuation  game,  it  was  publicly  announced  
26:1077:48446:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:that following the completion of each round, ownership of the good would be sold to the 
26:1078:48534:28:27:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:agent with the highest use value in the group at a price equal to her value.  In the resale 
26:1079:48626:27:28:90:527:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:treatment  with  EA  continuation  game,  it  was  publicly  announced  that  following  the  
26:1080:48720:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:completion  of  each  round,  ownership  of  the  good  would  be  sold  to  the  agent  with  the  
26:1081:48820:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:highest  use  value  in  the  group  at  a  price  equal  to  the  second  highest  use  value  of  all  
26:1082:48925:28:28:90:528:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:agents  in  the  group.13    In  the  baseline  no-resale  treatment,  several  examples  were  
26:1083:49021:28:27:89:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:provided  that  illustrated  the  irrationality  of  bidding  more  than  $10  above  a  received  
26:1084:49120:27:28:89:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:signal.    In  the  resale  treatments  several  examples  were  provided  that  illustrated  the  
26:1085:49219:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:workings of the resale market and how prices for resale exchange and earnings for each 
26:1086:49306:27:28:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidder  would  be  determined.14    Fifth,  individuals  participated  in  2  practice  rounds  of  
26:1087:49406:28:41:89:393:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidding to gain experience with the auction market and rules.   
26:1088:49470:41:7:234:237:281:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
26:1089:49518:7:16:90:524:274:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:13 Two important features of our experimental design that we should highlight include: i) our choice to limit 
26:1090:49628:16:12:90:525:258:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:participation  on  the  secondary  market  to  bidders  from  the  primary  auction  market  and  ii)  our  decision  to  
26:1091:49750:12:11:90:526:246:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:execute  trades  on  the  secondary  market  at  the  theoretical  benchmarks  for  both  the  OA  and  EA  game  of  
26:1092:49868:11:12:90:525:235:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:complete  information.    We  elected  to  limit  participation  on  the  secondary  market  to  maintain  consistency  
26:1093:49988:12:11:90:525:223:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:with theory and our naturally occurring data—the interior secondary market for timber in BC is comprised 
26:1094:50093:11:12:90:525:212:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:of bidders registered to participate in the primary auctions.  We elected to execute trade on the secondary 
26:1095:50201:12:11:90:524:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:market at the theoretical benchmarks to maintain consistency with our conceptual model.  The focus of this 
26:1096:50308:11:12:90:527:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:analysis  is  on  first-stage  bidding  strategies  rather  than  secondary  market  exchange.    Allowing  the  
26:1097:50421:12:11:90:526:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:endogenous  determination  of  prices  on  the  secondary  market  would  surely  have  an  influence  on  bidding  
26:1098:50537:11:12:90:528:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:strategies, as it is likely that rents would not be divided on the secondary market as predicated by theory.  
26:1099:50647:12:11:90:525:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:Anticipating  this,  bidders  would  adjust  first-stage  bidding  strategies.    We  hope  that  future  work  analyzes  
26:1100:50769:11:12:90:527:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:behavior  in  markets  where  prices  are  endogenously  determined  on  the  secondary  market  and  new  
26:1101:50876:12:7:90:368:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:participants are allowed to enter the second-stage continuation game. 
26:1102:50946:7:16:90:525:124:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:14  An  important  consideration  in  designing  our  auction  markets  was  the  issue  of  bankruptcy  and  bidder  
26:1103:51064:16:11:90:528:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:behavior.  Theoretically, bankruptcy was not an issue if subjects played the risk-neutral Nash equilibrium.  
26:1104:51173:11:12:90:526:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:However,  equilibrium  payouts  in  a  number  of  the  periods  were  low  enough  to  raise  concern  if  subjects  
26:1105:51291:12:11:90:526:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:determined  bids  with  a  degree  of  error.    For  reasons  outlined  in  Hansen  and  Lott  (1991),  we  decided  to  
26:1106:51413:11:36:90:527:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:employ an unlimited liability rule and allow subjects to have negative earnings for Part I of the experiment.   
27:1107:51525:36:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-26- 
27:1108:51530:0:27:125:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: In Step 3, subjects participated in the market.  Each market consisted of 10 rounds 
27:1109:51614:27:28:89:527:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:of  bidding  that  lasted  about  3  minutes  each.    After  each  3-minute  period,  a  monitor  
27:1110:51713:28:27:89:529:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:privately  gathered  each  subject’s  bidder  card  and  gave  the  bidder  a  second  card  
27:1111:51806:27:28:89:528:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:containing the subject’s final use value that was within [-$10, $10] of the original signal.  
27:1112:51900:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Once all bidder cards were collected, a monitor publicly announced all bids and awarded 
27:1113:51988:28:27:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:the  good  to  the  highest  bidder.    Final  use  values  were  publicly  announced  and,  in  the  
27:1114:52090:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:resale  treatment,  ownership  of  the  commodity  transferred  to  the  agent  with  highest  use  
27:1115:52190:28:27:89:127:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:value.   
27:1116:52199:27:28:125:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:It  should  be  noted  that  throughout  each  session  careful  attention  was  given  to  
27:1117:52291:28:28:89:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:prohibit communications between bidders that could induce collusive outcomes.  Step 4 
27:1118:52377:28:27:89:529:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:concluded   the   experiment   –   after   subjects   completed   the   Holt   and   Laury   (2002)   
27:1119:52479:27:28:89:516:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:experiment (described in Part II of this section), they were paid their earnings in private. 
27:1120:52572:28:27:125:528:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:This  simple  procedure  was  followed  in  each  of  three  treatments,  which  are  
27:1121:52658:27:28:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:summarized  in  Table  2.    Table  2  can  be  read  as  follows:    row  1,  column  2  of  Table  2  
27:1122:52762:28:27:89:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:contains  treatment  NR,  denoting  a  no-resale  auction  market  with  5  bidders,  who  each  
27:1123:52859:27:28:89:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:have  unit  demand  for  the  good.    Table  3  presents  buyer  induced  values  and  signals  for  
27:1124:52961:28:28:89:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:each market period.  All signals were drawn and assigned using the following procedure.  
27:1125:53050:28:27:89:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:We  first  drew  50  integer  numbers  on  the  uniform  distribution  between  [$10,  $40]  using  
27:1126:53150:27:28:89:529:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Excel’s  random  number  generator.    We  added  an  integer  drawn  on  the  uniform  
27:1127:53238:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:distribution  [-$10,  $10]  to  this  number  to  obtain  signal  values.    These  values  were  then  
27:1128:53342:27:28:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:assigned  so  that  unbeknownst  to  bidders,  in  each  session  (i)  every  bidder  received  the  
27:1129:53443:28:28:89:526:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:highest  signal  twice,  (ii)  each  bidder  received  the  highest  use  value  but  a  lower  ordered  
27:1130:53548:28:63:89:455:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:signal, and (iii) resale trade was potentially profitable in half of the periods. 
28:1131:53630:63:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-27- 
28:1132:53635:0:27:89:288:708:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Part II: The Holt-Laury Risk Experiment 
28:1133:53675:27:28:125:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: Upon completion of Part 1 of the session, instructions and a decision sheet were 
28:1134:53756:28:27:89:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:handed out for the second part of the experiment.  This second part was designed to elicit 
28:1135:53847:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:subjects’  risk  preferences.    In  this  part  of  the  session,  the  low-payoff  treatment  of  Holt  
28:1136:53953:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:and  Laury  (2002)  was  used  (see  Appendix  C  for  instructions).15  The treatment is based 
28:1137:54049:28:27:90:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:on ten choices between paired lotteries.  The paired choices are included in Appendix C.  
28:1138:54139:27:28:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:The  payoff  possibilities  for  Option  A,  $2.00  or  $1.60, are much less variable than those 
28:1139:54236:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:for  Option  B,  $3.85  or  $0.10,  which  was  considered  the  risky  option.    The  odds  of  
28:1140:54334:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:winning  the  higher  payoff  for  each  of  the  options  increased  with  each  decision,  and  the  
28:1141:54437:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:paired  choices  are  designed  to  determine  degrees  of  risk  aversion.    Holt  and  Laury  (p.  
28:1142:54539:28:27:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:1649)  provide  a  table  that  will  be  used  to  categorize  subjects’  CARA  risk  preference  
28:1143:54638:27:28:90:294:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:levels based on their ten decision choices. 
28:1144:54682:28:27:126:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:  After  the  instructions  were  read  and  questions  were  answered,  the  subjects  were  
28:1145:54776:27:28:90:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:asked  to  complete  their  decision  sheets  by  choosing  either  A  or  B  for  each  of  the  ten  
28:1146:54879:28:27:90:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:decisions.    The  subjects  were  instructed  that  one  of  the  decisions  would  be  randomly  
28:1147:54978:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:selected ex post and used to determine their payoffs.  Part of a deck of cards was used to 
28:1148:55069:28:28:89:524:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:determine payoffs, cards 2-10 and the Ace to represent “1”.  After each subject completed 
28:1149:55159:28:27:89:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:his or her decision sheet, a monitor would approach the desk and randomly draw a card 
28:1150:55245:27:34:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:twice,  once  to  select  which  of  the  ten  decisions  to  use,  and  a  second  time  to  determine  
28:1151:55350:34:8:234:237:178:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
28:1152:55398:8:16:90:525:170:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:15  We  elected  to  use  the  low-payoff  treatment  of  the  Holt  and  Laury  (2002)  experiment  to  measure  risk  
28:1153:55518:16:11:90:527:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:preference  since  the  domain  of  earnings  because  this  treatment  [$0.10  to  $3.85]  approximates  the  
28:1154:55629:11:12:90:522:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:equilibrium  domain  of  per  period  earnings  for  our  auction  markets.    We  also  collected  data  for  a  higher-
28:1155:55750:12:11:90:525:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:payoff treatment of the Holt and Laury (2002) experiment, where the domain of earnings [$0.40 to $15.40] 
28:1156:55855:11:12:90:526:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:approximates  the  equilibrium  domain  of  earnings  at  the  session  level  in  our  auction  markets.    In  what  
28:1157:55974:12:11:90:522:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:follows, we report only the empirical results for risk preference based upon individual response to the low-
28:1158:56082:11:12:90:524:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:payoff Holt and Laury (2002) design.  However, all tests and results are robust to the use of response to the 
28:1159:56192:12:11:90:200:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:higher-payoff experiment.  
28:1160:56219:11:36:90:93:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3: 
29:1161:56219:36:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-28- 
29:1162:56224:0:27:89:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:what  the  payoff  was  for  the  option  chosen,  A  or  B,  for  the  particular  decision  selected.    
29:1163:56331:27:28:89:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:After the first card was selected, it was placed back in the pile, the deck was reshuffled, 
29:1164:56423:28:27:89:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:and the second card was drawn.  For example, if the first draw was an Ace, then the first 
29:1165:56513:27:28:89:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:decision  choice  would  be  used.    Suppose  the  subject  selected  A  in  the  first  row.    The  
29:1166:56616:28:28:89:524:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:second draw would then be made.  If the Ace was drawn, the subject would win $2.00.  If 
29:1167:56704:28:27:89:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:a card numbered 2-10 was drawn, the subject would win $1.60.  The subjects were aware 
29:1168:56790:27:28:89:371:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:that each decision had an equal chance of being selected.   
29:1169:56850:28:27:125:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3: After all the subjects’ payoffs were determined, they combined their payoff from 
29:1170:56931:27:28:89:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Part  1  with  that  of  Part  2  to  compute  their  final  earnings.    The  final  payoffs  were  then  
29:1171:57038:28:28:89:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:verified against records maintained by a monitor, and subjects were paid privately in cash 
29:1172:57129:28:27:90:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:for  their  earnings.    Each  of  the  sessions  lasted  approximately  75  minutes  and  average  
29:1173:57229:27:28:90:224:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:earnings were roughly $13. 
29:1174:57256:28:27:90:380:377:144:g_d0_f5:144:g_d0_f5:Theoretical predictions for the laboratory auction markets   
29:1175:57317:27:28:126:531:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Figure   1   provides   theoretical   predictions   for   risk-neutral   bidders   in   our   
29:1176:57411:28:27:90:524:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:experimental markets conditioned upon the signal.  Across all but the lowest range of our 
29:1177:57501:27:28:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:signal  space  $0.00,  bidders  in  markets  with  resale  opportunities  represented  by  an  OA  
29:1178:57600:28:28:90:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:continuation  game  are  predicted  to  submit  bids  that  are  on  average  higher  than  those  
29:1179:57699:28:27:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:submitted by an equivalent bidder in a market without resale options.  These differences 
29:1180:57788:27:28:90:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:range  from  mere  pennies  for  signals  less  than  $5.00  to  a  maximum  of  about  $3.40  for  
29:1181:57888:28:27:90:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bids submitted in the signal range around $23.16  For signal ranges above $40.00 or below 
29:1182:57978:27:31:90:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:$20, the predicted differences in bids between the no-resale and resale treatments are less 
29:1183:58070:31:8:234:237:126:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:                                                 
29:1184:58118:8:18:90:525:118:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:16 The optimal bid functions were derived numerically.  Using the theory developed in Section III, we first 
29:1185:58226:18:15:90:524:100:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:calculated (, )RKxyand (, )RLxy on a grid with 0.1 increments.  Using interpolating functions, we then 
29:1186:58329:15:11:90:267:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:solved the respective differential equations. 
29:1187:58375:11:36:90:93:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3: 
30:1188:58375:36:0:295:318:38:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:-29- 
30:1189:58380:0:27:89:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:than  $2.75.    In  resale  treatments  represented  by  an  EA  continuation  game,  risk-neutral  
30:1190:58480:27:28:89:524:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:bidders are predicted to submit bids that are on average higher than those submitted by an 
30:1191:58571:28:27:89:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:equivalent  bidder  in  a  market  without  resale  at  ranges  of  our  signal  space  of  less  than  
30:1192:58675:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:$27.00.  For signals larger than  $27.00,  risk-neutral  bidders in our resale treatment with 
30:1193:58769:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:EA  continuation  game  are  predicted  to  submit  bids  that  are  on  average  less  than  those  
30:1194:58870:28:27:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:submitted  by  an  equivalent  bidder  in  the  no-resale  treatment.    These  differences  range  
30:1195:58970:27:28:89:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:from a maximum of $0.70 at a signal of approximately $20.00 to a minimum of $-0.56 at 
30:1196:59056:28:27:89:268:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:a signal of approximately $46.00.      
30:1197:59095:27:28:89:196:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:Experimental Results

35:1337:70459:28:28:90:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:(less  than  approximately  $21  for  risk-neutral  agents  and  up  to  approximately  $39  for
